Catholic parish church</figcaption></figure>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Surfing_in_Middle_Beach,_Isabela.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Surfing_in_Middle_Beach%2C_Isabela.jpg/220px-Surfing_in_Middle_Beach%2C_Isabela.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="145" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Surfing_in_Middle_Beach%2C_Isabela.jpg/330px-Surfing_in_Middle_Beach%2C_Isabela.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Surfing_in_Middle_Beach%2C_Isabela.jpg/440px-Surfing_in_Middle_Beach%2C_Isabela.jpg 2x" data-file-width="780" data-file-height="513" /></a><figcaption>An annual surfing competition is held at Middles Beach</figcaption></figure>\n<p><b>Isabela</b> (<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1177148991">.mw-parser-output .IPA-label-small{font-size:85%}.mw-parser-output .references .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .infobox .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .navbox .IPA-label-small{font-size:100%}</style><span class="IPA-label IPA-label-small">Spanish pronunciation:</span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="es-Latn-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">&#91;isa\xcb\x88\xce\xb2ela&#93;</a></span>) is a <a href="/wiki/Isabela_barrio-pueblo" title="Isabela barrio-pueblo">town</a> and <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Municipalities of Puerto Rico">municipality</a> of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> located in the north-western region of the island, north of <a href="/wiki/San_Sebasti%C3%A1n,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Sebasti\xc3\xa1n, Puerto Rico">San Sebasti\xc3\xa1n</a>; west of <a href="/wiki/Quebradillas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Quebradillas, Puerto Rico">Quebradillas</a>; and east of <a href="/wiki/Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico" title="Aguadilla, Puerto Rico">Aguadilla</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moca,_Puerto_Rico" title="Moca, Puerto Rico">Moca</a>. It is named in honor of Queen <a href="/wiki/Isabella_I_of_Castile" title="Isabella I of Castile">Isabella I of Castile</a>. Isabela is spread over 13 barrios and <a href="/wiki/Isabela_barrio-pueblo" title="Isabela barrio-pueblo">Isabela Pueblo</a>, which is the downtown area and administrative center. It is a principal part of the <a href="/wiki/Aguadilla-Isabela-San_Sebasti%C3%A1n_Metropolitan_Statistical_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="Aguadilla-Isabela-San Sebasti\xc3\xa1n Metropolitan Statistical Area">Aguadilla-Isabela-San Sebasti\xc3\xa1n Metropolitan Statistical Area</a>.\n</p>\n<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Nicknames">Nicknames</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isabela,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Nicknames"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The town is known as the <i>Jard\xc3\xadn del Noroeste</i> ("Garden of the Northwest"), because of the many <a href="/wiki/Wild_flowers" class="mw-redirect" title="Wild flowers">wild flowers</a> in its landscape. It is also known as <i>El Pueblo de los Quesitos de Hoja</i> ("Town of Leaf Cheeses") for its production of a typical fresh white cheese wrapped in banana plant leaves, reputed to be the best.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2007)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> It is also known as la <i>Ciudad de los Gallitos</i> or the "City of the Fighting Cocks." Since the 18th century, <a href="/wiki/Cock_fighting" class="mw-redirect" title="Cock fighting">cock fighting</a> was very common throughout the island, and the town became well known for the quality of its fighting cocks and special breeding and training techniques used by its people.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isabela,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The chief <i>Mabodamaca</i>, one of the most important chieftains of the island of Borinquen (<a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_language" title="Ta\xc3\xadno language">Ta\xc3\xadno</a> for <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>) during the first decades of the 16th century, ruled the region of the \'Guajataca\' (Ta\xc3\xadno name for the northwestern region of Puerto Rico) where Isabela was founded. Although the actual date of the origins of the first <a href="/wiki/Spanish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Spanish colonization of the Americas">Spanish</a> settlement is not precisely known, a small settlement/hermitage is known to have existed by the end of the 17th century or beginning of the 18th century in a great extension of land into what encompass today the municipalities of Isabela, <a href="/wiki/Camuy,_Puerto_Rico" title="Camuy, Puerto Rico">Camuy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quebradillas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Quebradillas, Puerto Rico">Quebradillas</a>. The settlement was bordered to the east with the shoreline of the <a href="/wiki/Guajataca_River" title="Guajataca River">Guajataca River</a> and was located on the grounds of an earlier Ta\xc3\xadno settlement.\n</p><p>Around 1725, Jos\xc3\xa9 Antonio de Mendiz\xc3\xa1bal y Azares, Governor of the Island of Puerto Rico granted authorization to base a population on the existing hermitage/village. Its given name, <b>San Antonio de La Tuna</b>, derives from the <a href="/wiki/Avocation" title="Avocation">avocation</a> of the Spanish settlers to the saint <a href="/wiki/Anthony_of_Padua" title="Anthony of Padua">Anthony of Padua</a> and in honor of a wild <a href="/wiki/Cactus" title="Cactus">cactus</a> growing in the region (Tuna is the Spanish term for <a href="/wiki/Cactus" title="Cactus">cactus</a>). At the end of the 18th century <i>San Antonio de la Tuna</i> had a church, more than sixty houses, and almost 1,200 inhabitants, which was a considerable population for those times.\n</p><p>Prompted by economic and health factors, the decision to relocate the hermitage to a more favorable location was pursued. Around 1818, the village obtained authorization from then Governor <a href="/w/index.php?title=Salvador_Mel%C3%A9ndez&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Salvador Mel\xc3\xa9ndez (page does not exist)">Salvador Mel\xc3\xa9ndez</a> to transfer the population to a new location closer to the coast. Mel\xc3\xa9ndez approved the transfer request and a new town was founded the following year on May 21, 1819. In the same year the construction of the church began, and was finished in 1824. In 1918 the church was damaged during a strong earthquake that affected the western region of the island, it was rebuilt soon after.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Puerto Rico was ceded by <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> in the aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War">Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War</a> under the terms of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_of_1898" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Paris of 1898">Treaty of Paris of 1898</a> and became a territory of the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>. In 1899, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_War" title="United States Department of War">United States Department of War</a> conducted a <a href="/wiki/Census" title="Census">census</a> of Puerto Rico finding that the population of Isabela was 14,888.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>On September 20, 2017, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Maria</a> struck Puerto Rico. In Isabela, the hurricane caused destruction of homes and infrastructure. Maria caused structural damage to the nearby <a href="/wiki/Guajataca_Lake" title="Guajataca Lake">Guajataca Reservoir</a> and thousands of people were evacuated from their homes.<sup id="cite_ref-ELN_Isabela_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ELN_Isabela-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 1910\xe2\x80\x931930<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><br />1930\xe2\x80\x931950<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 1960\xe2\x80\x932000<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 2010<sup id="cite_ref-2010_Census_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010_Census-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 2020<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<p>In the 2010 census, there were 45,631 people in the city. This represents an increase of more than 1,000 from the 2000 census.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The population density was 825.1 inhabitants per square mile (318.6/km<sup>2</sup>). The 2020 census indicated the municipality had 42,943 residents, a decline of over 3,000.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Geography">Geography</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isabela,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Geography"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Isabela is a hybrid town of sorts, with the rarity of being a coastline city that has beaches but is also known for its mountains (with peaks of over 1,000&#160;ft [300&#160;m] above sea level), rivers (surface and submarine), lakes, caves (surface and submarine), cliffs, coastal flats and forests (including <a href="/wiki/Mangrove" title="Mangrove">mangroves</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-PR_Ency_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PR_Ency-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Geographically, the municipality of Isabela belongs to the Northern Coastal Plains and the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Karst_(Puerto_Rico)" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Karst (Puerto Rico)">Northern Karst</a> region. Running through the south, the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Aymam%C3%B3n_Mountains&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Aymam\xc3\xb3n Mountains (page does not exist)">Aymam\xc3\xb3n Mountains</a>, a prolongation of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jaicoa_Mountain_Range&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Jaicoa Mountain Range (page does not exist)">Jaicoa Mountain Range</a> that begins in the neighboring town of <a href="/wiki/Aguadilla" class="mw-redirect" title="Aguadilla">Aguadilla</a>, boasts peaks of over 1,000 feet (300&#160;m) above sea level. The most prominent hills that are part of these mountains are La Bandera (<a href="/wiki/Galateo_Alto" title="Galateo Alto">Galateo Alto</a> ward) at 1,207&#160;ft (368&#160;m); La Silla (<a href="/wiki/Arenales_Altos" title="Arenales Altos">Arenales Alto</a> ward) at 1,106&#160;ft (337&#160;m); El Sombrero (in <a href="/wiki/Galateo_Alto" title="Galateo Alto">Galateo Alto</a>) at 1,083 feet (330&#160;m); Indio (<a href="/wiki/Planas" title="Planas">Planas</a> ward) at 1,017 feet (310&#160;m); and Monte Encantado (in Arenales Altos) at 919 feet (280&#160;m) of elevation above sea level. The central part of the territory consists mostly of flatlands, the mountains do not surpass 656 feet (200&#160;m) in height and the coastline flats (<a href="/wiki/Bajura,_Isabela,_Puerto_Rico" title="Bajura, Isabela, Puerto Rico">Bajuras</a>) are slightly above sea level.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Barrios">Barrios</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isabela,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Barrios"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Isabela,_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Isabela%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png/220px-Isabela%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="230" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Isabela%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png/330px-Isabela%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Isabela%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png/440px-Isabela%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png 2x" data-file-width="1100" data-file-height="1148" /></a><figcaption>Subdivisions of Isabela</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Like all municipalities of Puerto Rico, Isabela is subdivided into <a href="/wiki/Barrios_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Barrios of Puerto Rico">barrios</a>. The municipal buildings, central square and large Catholic church are located in a barrio referred to as <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">"el pueblo"</i></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-Pico_1969_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pico_1969-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Law2015_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law2015-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2010_Census_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010_Census-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1184024115">.mw-parser-output .div-col{margin-top:0.3em;column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .div-col-small{font-size:90%}.mw-parser-output .div-col-rules{column-rule:1px solid #aaa}.mw-parser-output .div-col dl,.mw-parser-output .div-col ol,.mw-parser-output .div-col ul{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .div-col li,.mw-parser-output .div-col dd{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}</style><div class="div-col" style="column-width: 15em;">\n<ol><li><a href="/wiki/Arenales_Altos" title="Arenales Altos">Arenales Altos</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Arenales_Bajos" title="Arenales Bajos">Arenales Bajos</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Bajura,_Isabela,_Puerto_Rico" title="Bajura, Isabela, Puerto href="/wiki/Galateo_Alto" title="Galateo Alto">Galateo Alto</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Galateo_Bajo" title="Galateo Bajo">Galateo Bajo</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Guayabos" title="Planas">Planas</a></li></ol>\n</div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Sectors">Sectors</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isabela,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Sectors"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Barrios (which are, in contemporary times, roughly comparable to  <a href="/wiki/Minor_civil_divisions" class="mw-redirect" title="Minor civil divisions">minor civil divisions</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-Barrio-Pueblo_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Barrio-Pueblo-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and subbarrios,<sup id="cite_ref-Census_map_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census_map-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> are further subdivided into smaller areas called <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">sectores</i></span> (<i>sectors</i> in English). The types of <i>sectores</i> may vary, from normally <i>sector</i> to <i>urbanizaci\xc3\xb3n</i> to <i>reparto</i> to <i>barriada</i> to <i>residencial</i>, among others.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Law_1-2001_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law_1-2001-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Special_Communities">Special Communities</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isabela,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Special Communities"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1236090951">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .hatnote{display:none!important}}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Office_for_Socioeconomic_and_Community_Development" title="Puerto Rico Office for Socioeconomic and Community Development">Puerto Rico Office for Socioeconomic and Community Development</a></div>\n<p><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Comunidades Especiales de Puerto Rico</i></span> (Special Communities of Puerto Rico) are marginalized communities whose citizens are experiencing a certain amount of <a href="/wiki/Social_exclusion" title="Social exclusion">social exclusion</a>. A map shows these communities occur in nearly every municipality of the commonwealth. Of the 742 places that were on the list in 2014, the following barrios, communities, sectors, or neighborhoods were in Isabela: Cerro del Sombrero in Arenales Alto, Pueblo Nuevo in Arenales Bajos, Barriada Corchado, Comunidad Poncito in Llanadas, Sector Las Parcelas and Sector Pastillo and Sector San Antonio de la Tuna in Coto, Sector Capiro and Sector Corea in Galateo Alto, Sector El Ramal in Guerrero, Parcelas Nuevas and Parcelas Viejas in Mora Guerrero, Comunidad Cristal, Sector Planas, Media Cuerda, Parcelas Jobos, Santa B\xc3\xa1rbara, Sector El Ca\xc3\xb1\xc3\xb3n, Sector El Verdum, Sector La Mantilla, Sector La Marina, Sector La Mina, Sector La Sierra, Tocones, and Villa Pesquera.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wordpress.com_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wordpress.com-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Climate">Climate</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span mw-heading2"><h2 id="Tourism">Tourism</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isabela,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Tourism"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/An_arcuate_beach_in_Isabela%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/220px-An_arcuate_beach_in_Isabela%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="142" /></a><figcaption>Centro Empresarial Playero \xe2\x80\x93 Villa Pesquera</figcaption></figure>\n<p>To stimulate local tourism, the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Tourism_Company" title="Puerto Rico Tourism Company">Puerto Rico Tourism Company</a> launched the <i>Voy Turistiendo</i> ("I\'m Touring") campaign, with a passport book and website. The Isabela page lists <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Playa Montones</i></span>, <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Tunel de Guajataca</i></span>, and <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Mabodamaca</i></span>, as places of interest.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Landmarks_and_places_of_interest">Landmarks and places of interest</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isabela,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Landmarks and places of interest"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>According to a news article by <a href="/wiki/Primera_Hora_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Primera Hora (Puerto Rico)">Primera Hora</a>, there are 12 beaches in Isabela including <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Jobos</i></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\nThe main attractions of Isabela include:\n</p>\n<ul><li>El Pozo Brujo (The Bewitched Well)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Jobos_Beach" title="Jobos Beach">Jobos Beach</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Pozo_de_Jacinto" title="Pozo de Jacinto">Pozo de Jacinto</a></li>\n<li>Montones Beach</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hermitage_of_San_Antonio_de_Padua_de_la_Tuna" title="Hermitage of San Antonio de Padua de la Tuna">San Antonio de la Tuna Ruins</a></li>\n<li>Punta Sardina</li>\n<li>La Poza de Punta Sandina</li>\n<li>La Princesa Beach &amp; Blow Hole</li>\n<li>Villa Pesquera</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Guajataca" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Guajataca">R\xc3\xado Guajataca</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Guajataca_Tunnel" title="Guajataca Tunnel">Guajataca Tunnel</a></li>\n<li>La Cara del Indio (The Indian\'s Face)</li>\n<li>La Posita de Teodoro</li>\n<li>Middles Beach<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>La Posita de Montones</li>\n<li>Casa Parroquial</li>\n<li>Parroquia San Antonio de la Tuna</li>\n<li>La Posita de la Princesa</li>\n<li>Shore Island Beach</li>\n<li>Paseo Lineal</li>\n<li>San Antonio de la Tuna Museum</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/La_Pocita_de_las_Golondrinas_Beach" title="La Pocita de las Golondrinas Beach">La Pocita de Isabela (Poza de Teodoro)</a></li>\n<li>La Cueva de las Golondrinas</li>\n<li>Cueva los Vientos (Bosque Guajataca)</li>\n<li>Photo Museum of Isabela</li>\n<li>Alcaldia de Isabela</li>\n<li>The Pink House (Casa Rosada), (Demolished in 2014 by the Municipality to be transformed into a museum) <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.facebook.com/photo.php?fbid=10152446052608775&amp;set=o.145605908845156&amp;type=3&amp;theater">Lewiz Menz</a></li>\n<li>Bajura Beach also known as Shacks Beach</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Economy">Economy</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isabela,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Economy"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Agriculture">Agriculture</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isabela,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Agriculture"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The early economy of the hermitage had been based mainly on cattle [ranching], its derivative products and hogs products, but trading was limited due to many factors: its inland location and topography. The settlement was posted above a hill overlooking the river (now <a href="/wiki/Guajataca_River" title="Guajataca River">River <i>Guajataca</i></a>) which made it difficult to use the river as a trading route, as did the location\'s propensity to disease and outbreaks.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>After the transfer to the present Isabela location the economic realities that resulted from the new land and property opportunities that were readily available, the healthier environment formed due to the wide open plains and prevalent northern winds, and the proximity to the coast and the natural sea port at the bay of Punta Sardina prompted for the diversification of the agricultural products and an increase in trade. The cultivation of <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">sugarcane</a>, coffee, tobacco, cotton, Cassava/yuca, coconut and other fruits was stimulated further. Isabela continued to flourish until recent years due to the island\'s economic crisis, the closing of important factories and the rising crime rate.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Industry">Industry</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isabela,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Industry"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Isabela also has a hi-tech plant, a higher education institution, a world-renowned agricultural research center and a major shopping center, Plaza Isabela.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Culture">Culture</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isabela,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Culture"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Festivals_and_events">Festivals and events</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isabela,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Festivals and events"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Isabela celebrates its <a href="/wiki/Fiestas_patronales_in_Puerto_Rico" title="Fiestas patronales in Puerto Rico">patron saint</a> festival in June. The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Fiestas Patronales de San Antonio de Padua</i></span> is a religious and cultural celebration that generally features parades, games, artisans, amusement rides, regional food, and live entertainment.<sup id="cite_ref-PR_Ency_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PR_Ency-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-J.D._2006_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-J.D._2006-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Other festivals and events celebrated in Isabela include:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Three Kings day \xe2\x80\x93 January \xe2\x80\x93 organized by La Casa de la Cultura Isabelina Inc (non profit cultural organization) honoring the wiseman (Reyes Magos) tradition represented by the "Reyes Cantores Isabelinos".</li>\n<li>Isabela Cock Fight Festival \xe2\x80\x93 February</li>\n<li>Textile Festival \xe2\x80\x93 May</li>\n<li>Puerto Rock Steady Music Festival \xe2\x80\x93 May</li>\n<li>Weave Festival \xe2\x80\x93 May</li>\n<li>Kite Festival \xe2\x80\x93 May</li>\n<li>Isabela Muscle Cars Auto Show \xe2\x80\x93 August</li>\n<li>Isabela International Tango Festival \xe2\x80\x93 August <sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>Las Noches de la Puertorrique\xc3\xb1idad del colegio San Antonio \xe2\x80\x93 November<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Feria de Autos Clasicos y Antiguos del Noroeste Inc.</i></span> \xe2\x80\x93 November</li>\n<li>Isabela Has Flavor \xe2\x80\x93 November<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Holy_Innocents%27_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="Holy Innocents&#39; Day">Holy Innocents\' Day</a> \xe2\x80\x93 December</li>\n<li>Caroling "Escuadr\xc3\xb3n" (Marina) \xe2\x80\x93 December</li>\n<li>Caroling "Siempreviva" (Marina) \xe2\x80\x93 January</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Sports">Sports</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isabela,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Sports"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Isabela is also well known for its world-class <a href="/wiki/Surfing" title="Surfing">surfing</a> spots, and hosted two <a href="/wiki/World_surfing_champion" class="mw-redirect" title="World surfing champion">World Cup Surfing Championships</a>, as well as some of the <a href="/wiki/Rip_Curl_Pro" title="Rip Curl Pro">Rip Curl Pro</a> competitions.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Isabela had a <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a> team that played at the <a href="/wiki/Jose_%22Buga%22_Abreu_Coliseum" class="mw-redirect" title="Jose &quot;Buga&quot; Abreu Coliseum">Jose "Buga" Abreu Coliseum</a>, the Isabela Roosters ("Gallitos de Isabela") Between the mid-1970s and mid-1980s, the Bantams were serious championship contenders. In the late 1970s their star player, Mickey Coll, died in a motorcycle accident. The team\'s first home court was named after him. The Bantams were Isabela\'s home team until October 2005 when they moved the franchise to Guaynabo. \n</p><p>The Playeras, a female volleyball team, played in Isabela for 2 seasons until they also moved to Aguadilla becoming Las Divas.\n</p><p>The Isabela Muscle Cars Club, celebrating annual events since 2002, is a popular event in Isabela.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> On August 28, 2016, the club celebrated their 15th Anniversary at the <i>Coliseum Jose "Buga" Abreu</i>.\n</p><p>The town also has its own classic car club, called <i>"Club de Autos Clasicos y Antiguos del Noroeste"</i> (Classic and Old Car Club from Northwest). They also celebrate their own Exhibition of Classic Cars at the coliseum in November.\n</p><p>The local basketball team was called the <i>"Gallitos"</i> ("Little Cocks," in reference to the slim, lightweight body of the fighting variety) due to the town\'s fame for quality fighting cocks. The name was translated literally into English as "Bantams", a variety of dwarf cocks.\n</p><p>The town has a cockfighting arena, traditionally called a <i>gallera</i>. Fights were customarily held on Sunday mornings, and the bets and stakes were controlled by the government of Puerto Rico. Prizes were paid based on the fighting record of the cocks. A law prohibiting cockfighting in the U.S. and its territories went into effect in early 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Isabela has amateur baseball teams. Also, Isabela is well known for its Fine Step Horses ("Caballos de <a href="/wiki/Paso_Fino" title="Paso Fino">Paso Fino</a>") and its world class board, wind and kite surfing spots.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Government">Government</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isabela,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Government"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mayoralty_in_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Mayoralty in Puerto Rico">Mayoralty in Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<p>Like all municipalities in <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, Isabela is administered by a mayor. The current mayor is Miguel "Ricky" M\xc3\xa9ndez P\xc3\xa9rez, from the <a href="/wiki/Popular_Democratic_Party_of_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Popular Democratic Party of Puerto Rico">Popular Democratic Party</a> (PPD).<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> M\xc3\xa9ndez was elected in the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_general_election,_2020" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rican general election, 2020">2020 general election</a>.\n</p><p>The city belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Senatorial_district_IV" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rico Senatorial district IV">Puerto Rico Senatorial district IV</a>, which is represented by two senators. In 2012, <a href="/wiki/Mar%C3%ADa_Teresa_Gonz%C3%A1lez" title="Mar\xc3\xada Teresa Gonz\xc3\xa1lez">Mar\xc3\xada Teresa Gonz\xc3\xa1lez</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gilberto_Rodr%C3%ADguez" title="Gilberto Rodr\xc3\xadguez">Gilberto Rodr\xc3\xadguez</a> were elected as District Senators.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Transportation">Transportation</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isabela,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Transportation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>There are 5 bridges in Isabela.<sup id="cite_ref-bridge_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bridge-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Symbols">Symbols</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isabela,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Symbols"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">municipio</i></span> has an official flag and coat of arms.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Flag">Flag</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isabela,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Flag"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Isabela.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="The flag resembles the coat of arms." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Flag_of_Isabela.svg/165px-Flag_of_Isabela.svg.png" decoding="async" width="165" height="110" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Flag_of_Isabela.svg/248px-Flag_of_Isabela.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Flag_of_Isabela.svg/330px-Flag_of_Isabela.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="200" /></a><figcaption>The Isabela flag</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Isabela\'s flag derives its design, colors and symbolism from its coat of arms. It consists of three horizontal stripes of equal width. The top and bottom stripe are yellow and the center one green. The coat of arms may be superposed on the green stripe in the center.<sup id="cite_ref-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Coat_of_arms">Coat of arms</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isabela,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Coat of arms"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Escudo_de_Isabela,_Puerto_Rico.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Escudo_de_Isabela%2C_Puerto_Rico.svg/200px-Escudo_de_Isabela%2C_Puerto_Rico.svg.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="289" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Escudo_de_Isabela%2C_Puerto_Rico.svg/300px-Escudo_de_Isabela%2C_Puerto_Rico.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Escudo_de_Isabela%2C_Puerto_Rico.svg/400px-Escudo_de_Isabela%2C_Puerto_Rico.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="323" data-file-height="466" /></a><figcaption>Coat of arms of Isabela</figcaption></figure>\n<p>The town\'s <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms" title="Coat of arms">coat of arms</a>, dated 1819, is divided an <a href="/wiki/Olive_tree" class="mw-redirect" title="Olive tree">olive tree</a> in its center, symbolizes the first inhabitants of Isabela and of the island of Puerto Rico, the <a href="/wiki/Igneris" class="mw-redirect" title="Igneris">Igneris</a> Indians. The gold represents the <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno" title="Ta\xc3\xadno">Ta\xc3\xadno</a> Indians (they made extensive use of gold), who lived in this area about two hundred years before the discovery of the island. The gold bell represented in the center stripe between two cactus is a symbol of the town of <b>San Antonio de la Tuna</b>. The two cocks represent the bravery of the inhabitants and Isabela\'s famous <a href="/wiki/Cockfight" class="mw-redirect" title="Cockfight">fighting cocks</a>. The horse represents the cattle wealth of the region and honors the fine step horses (<a href="/wiki/Paso_Fino" title="Paso Fino">Paso Fino</a>) for which Isabela is known.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The coat of arms is embellished with a <a href="/wiki/Mural_crown" title="Mural crown">mural crown</a> having three towers, the standard emblem at the time for formally established \'pueblos\' (townships) under Spanish rule. The revised mural crown with five towers represents a city, but historically, only 11 communities<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> in Puerto Rico were conferred this title when under Spanish rule.\n</p><p>On the occasion of the celebration of 186 years of Isabela it was necessary to adopt an ordinance to establish properly the historical veracity and heraldic elements of the emblazoned shield and official seal of the City of Isabela. The following information was drafted pursuant to Ordinance Number 3, series 2005\xe2\x80\x932006 and approved by the Municipal Legislature on August 5, 2005:\n</p><p>"The Mural Crown: Current mural crown that has the coat of Isabela has three towers. Due to population increase of over 50,000 inhabitants who had Isabela in this last decade, the HUD office in Washington DC, conferred status as a "city" to Isabela last year. Given this demographic reality and focused on the mural crown that represents the spirit of unity and growth of the inhabitants of our city of Isabela, we understand appropriate that the crown mural consists of "five" distinct towers that symbolize the passage from town to city."<sup id="cite_ref-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Notable_people">Notable people</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isabela,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Notable people"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9lix_Mantilla_(baseball)" title="F\xc3\xa9lix Mantilla (baseball)">F\xc3\xa9lix Mantilla (baseball)</a>, former All-Star and World Series champion baseball player for the <a href="/wiki/Milwaukee_Braves" title="Milwaukee Braves">Milwaukee Braves</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mets" title="New York Mets">New York Mets</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston Red Sox</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/V%C3%ADctor_Manuelle" title="V\xc3\xadctor Manuelle">V\xc3\xadctor Manuelle</a>, a world-renowned salsa singer. His parents are from Isabela, and he has featured his hometown in several music videos.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Manuel_Corchado_y_Juarbe" title="Manuel Corchado y Juarbe">Manuel Corchado y Juarbe</a>,(September 12, 1840 \xe2\x80\x93 November 30, 1884) was a poet, journalist and politician who defended the abolition of slavery and the establishment of a university in Puerto Rico.</li>\n<li><b>Noel Epinanio Estrada Su\xc3\xa1rez</b> (June 4, 1918 \xe2\x80\x93 December 1, 1979) was a  <a href="/wiki/Composer" title="Composer">composer</a>. He was the author of "<a href="/wiki/En_mi_Viejo_San_Juan" title="En mi Viejo San Juan">En mi Viejo San Juan</a>", a song "widely known around the world".</li>\n<li><b>Vicente Geigel Polanco</b> (May 1, 1904 \xe2\x80\x93 April 30, 1979) was a lawyer, writer and a former <a href="/wiki/Attorney_General_of_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Attorney General of Puerto Rico">Attorney General of Puerto Rico</a>.</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="See_also">See also</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a
